" class=3D"type-no-paragraph-margins" style=3D"font-size:0px;padding:0;padd=
ing-top:24px;padding-bottom:12px;word-break:break-word;"><div style=3D"font=
-family:'Nib Pro', Arial;font-size:24px;font-weight:600;line-height:32px;te=
xt-align:left;color:#000000;"><p>US regulators rush to limit banking contag=
ion after Silicon Valley Bank=E2=80=99s collapse</p></div></td></tr><tr><td=
 align=3D"left" style=3D"font-size:0px;padding:0;word-break:break-word;"><d=
iv style=3D"font-family:'Capsule Sans Text', Arial;font-size:15px;font-weig=
ht:400;letter-spacing:-0.1px;line-height:24px;text-align:left;color:#000000=
;"><p><strong>From ski resort to last resort=E2=80=A6</strong> Earlier this=
 month <strong>Silicon Valley Bank</strong> hosted a =E2=80=9Csnow summit=
=E2=80=9D for tech CFOs at the Deer Valley ski resort in Utah. Last week, S=
VB tried to borrow from the Fed =E2=80=94 a lender of last resort =E2=80=94=
 to avoid collapsing (spoiler: it still collapsed). Here=E2=80=99s a high-l=
evel recap of the second-largest bank failure in US history:</p><ul style=
=3D"padding-left: 18px;"><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;"><strong>Who:</s=
trong> Silicon Valley Bank was the go-to for tech startups, servicing about=
 half of America=E2=80=99s venture-backed tech companies.</li><li style=3D"=
margin-bottom: 12px;"><strong>Rise:</strong> SVB was flooded with deposits =
in 2021 as startups easily raised venture cash in an extra-low-interest-rat=
e environment, parking their funds at SVB.</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: =
12px;"><strong>Problem:</strong> Banks largely make $$ by making loans, but=
 SVB=E2=80=99s clients were already flush with cash. Plus, interest rates o=
n loans (especially short term) were super low.</li><li style=3D"margin-bot=
tom: 12px;"><strong>=E2=80=9CSolution=E2=80=9D:</strong> To earn a slightly=
 higher interest rate on its loans, SVB invested most of its deposits into =
US Treasury bonds with long durations (think: 10+ years).</li><li style=3D"=
margin-bottom: 12px;"><strong>Risk:</strong> If interest rates soared, the =
value of SVB=E2=80=99s bond portfolio would plunge (because its old bonds w=
ould be paying out at lower interest rates).</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom=
: 12px;"><strong>Result:</strong> Interest rates did in fact soar. The mark=
et value of SVB=E2=80=99s bonds plummeted by $15B (and its savvy customers =
paid attention).</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;"><strong>Re-tweet:</=
strong> SVB=E2=80=99s close-knit clients chatted and pulled their cash out =
at the same time (on Thursday alone, they tried to withdraw $42B =E2=80=94 =
a quarter of SVB=E2=80=99s total deposits).</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom:=

<strong>From ski resort to last resort=E2=80=A6</strong> Earlier this month=
 <strong>Silicon Valley Bank</strong> hosted a =E2=80=9Csnow summit=E2=80=
=9D for tech CFOs at the Deer Valley ski resort in Utah. Last week, SVB tri=
ed to borrow from the Fed =E2=80=94 a lender of last resort =E2=80=94 to av=
oid collapsing (spoiler: it still collapsed). Here=E2=80=99s a high-level r=
ecap of the second-largest bank failure in US history:</p><ul style=3D"padd=
ing-left: 18px;"><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;"><strong>Who:</strong> S=
ilicon Valley Bank was the go-to for tech startups, servicing about half of=
 America=E2=80=99s venture-backed tech companies.</li><li style=3D"margin-b=
ottom: 12px;"><strong>Rise:</strong> SVB was flooded with deposits in 2021 =
as startups easily raised venture cash in an extra-low-interest-rate enviro=
nment, parking their funds at SVB.</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;"><=
strong>Problem:</strong> Banks largely make $$ by making loans, but SVB=E2=
=80=99s clients were already flush with cash. Plus, interest rates on loans=
 (especially short term) were super low.</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12=
px;"><strong>=E2=80=9CSolution=E2=80=9D:</strong> To earn a slightly higher=
 interest rate on its loans, SVB invested most of its deposits into US Trea=
sury bonds with long durations (think: 10+ years).</li><li style=3D"margin-=
bottom: 12px;"><strong>Risk:</strong> If interest rates soared, the value o=
f SVB=E2=80=99s bond portfolio would plunge (because its old bonds would be=
 paying out at lower interest rates).</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;=
"><strong>Result:</strong> Interest rates did in fact soar. The market valu=
e of SVB=E2=80=99s bonds plummeted by $15B (and its savvy customers paid at=
tention).</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;"><strong>Re-tweet:</strong>=
 SVB=E2=80=99s close-knit clients chatted and pulled their cash out at the =
same time (on Thursday alone, they tried to withdraw $42B =E2=80=94 a quart=
er of SVB=E2=80=99s total deposits).</li><li style=3D"margin-bottom: 12px;"=
><strong>Reckoning:</strong> SVB ultimately couldn=E2=80=99t meet withdrawa=
l requests, the FDIC took control and declared it insolvent, and panic ensu=
ed (<strong><a href=3D"https://sg.robinhood.com/ls/click?upn=3D6fntGirSE5se=
